The First Zahiri Argument and Its Refutation
Zahiri claim and first argument with refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first argument used by the Zahiris to deny attributes beyond the seven and how it is refuted by denying both premises.

Core Idea
Lack of proof does not entail denial — both claims must be proved.

The Zahiris argued that since there is no evidence for additional attributes, they must be denied. However, this argument rests on two unproven premises. In this lesson, we examine the reasoning and the refutation that challenges each premise.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a claim, a reason with two premises, and a refutation that denies those premises.
The refutation is brief: 'denying both premises'.
2
Identify the two premises
The Zahiri argument has two premises: (1) there is no evidence for additional attributes, and (2) everything without evidence must be denied. Find these in the text.
3
Understand the refutation
The refutation denies both premises. Ask yourself: why might there still be evidence? And why should lack of evidence automatically mean denial? This challenges the logical necessity.
This highlights a key principle in kalam: absence of proof is not proof of absence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث السابع : في صفات اختلف فيها يعني اختلف فيها أهل الحق القائلون بالصفات الأزلية . زعم بعض الظاهرية أنه لا صفة الله تعالى وراء السبعة المذكورة لوجهين : أحدهما : أنه لا دليل عليه وكل ما لا دليل عليه يجب نفيه، ورد بمنع المقدمتين. وثانيهما: أنا مكلفون بكمال المعرفة، وذلك بمعرفة الذات وجميع الصفات فلم كانت له صفات أخرى لعرفناها معشر العارفين الكاملين واللازم منتف بالضرورة وبأنه لا طريق إلى معرفة الصفات سوى الاستدلال بالأفعال، والتنزيه عن النقائص، وهما لا يدلان على صفة أخرى، ورد بالمنع بل التكليف بقدر الوسع . ولو سلم فما أدريك أن الكاملين لم يعرفوا صفة أخرى ، ولا نسلم أنه لا طريق سوى ما ذكرتم . أليس الشرع طريقاً قويماً، وصراطاً مستقياً ؟
The seventh investigation: concerning attributes that are disputed, meaning the people of truth who affirm the eternal attributes disagreed among themselves. Some of the Zahiris claimed that there is no attribute of Allah Almighty beyond the seven mentioned, based on two aspects: First: there is no evidence for it, and everything for which there is no evidence must be denied—refuted by denying both premises. Second: we are obligated to perfect knowledge, and that is by knowing the essence and all attributes; so if He had other attributes, we, the community of perfect knowers, would know them, and the consequent is necessarily negated—and because there is no way to know attributes except by inference from actions and transcendence of imperfections, and both do not indicate another attribute—refuted by denying it, rather the obligation is according to capacity. And if it were granted, what makes you think that the perfect knowers did not know another attribute? And we do not concede that there is no way other than what you mentioned. Is not the Shari'ah a straight path and a direct way?
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Zahiri position that God has no attributes beyond the seven well-known ones. The author first states the Zahiri claim and their two proofs: (1) no proof exists for additional attributes, and whatever has no proof must be denied, and (2) we are obligated to perfect knowledge, which requires knowing the essence and all attributes; if there were others, the perfect knowers would know them. The author refutes both: first, by denying the premises (the claim that there is no proof and the claim that lack of proof necessitates denial). Second, by denying that the obligation is to know all attributes – rather, obligation is according to capacity. Furthermore, he questions: 'What makes you think the perfect knowers did not know another attribute?' And he denies that there is no way to know attributes except through actions and transcendence; rather, the Shari'ah is a straight path and a direct way.

Key Terms
الظاهرية
السبعة المذكورة
دليل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If there is no evidence for something, it must be false or non-existent.
Correction: Lack of evidence is not a proof of absence. The Zahiri argument fails because its premises are not necessarily true; there may be evidence or the rule itself may be invalid.

Checkpoint
What does the refutation of the first Zahiri argument consist of?
A) Proving that there is evidence for additional attributes.
B) Denying both premises of the argument.
C) Accepting the premises but rejecting the conclusion.
D) Ignoring the argument entirely.

Key Takeaway
The first Zahiri argument is refuted because its two premises are not established; lack of evidence does not automatically warrant denial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself demanding strict proof for every aspect of your faith before you accept it? Which of your beliefs would survive if you applied that standard consistently?
?
The refutation here simply denies both premises without elaboration. In your own spiritual journey, has there been a time when a simple, direct rejection of a flawed principle helped you see the truth more clearly? Describe that moment.
?
The Zahiris assumed that lack of evidence justifies denial. In your life, are there matters of belief or practice that you hold without 'proof' but out of trust in revelation and scholars? How do you reconcile that with a desire for certainty?
